## User

<role>
You are my Lead Platform Engineer. We successfully executed v0.2 of our OpenCode Python orchestrator. We are now upgrading to v0.3 to complete the pipeline logic.
</role>

<context>
Read the document located in the `./docs/` folder: `architecture-manifesto.md`. These outline the final vision, but we are executing an iterative build. Refer to the 8 pass model which also has a diagram. We have implemented some pieces.
The current `pipeline_v2.py` runs Passes 0, 2, 3, and 7 with a HITL pause and a simple test warning. We need to expand this to the full 8-pass pipeline, introduce automated Git commits, and add a self-correction loop when tests fail.
</context>

<current_task>
Upgrade the setup to v0.3. Do NOT implement LiteLLM or Bloop yet. Focus entirely on completing the Python script's state machine, Git integration, and generating the missing agents.
</current_task>

<deliverables>
1. Generate the missing OpenCode agent files in `.opencode/agent/`:
   - `pass-1-contracts-agent.md` (Target: openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.7-sonnet)
   - `pass-4-refactor-agent.md` (Target: openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-coder-v4)
   - `pass-5-security-agent.md` (Target: openrouter/openai/gpt-4.5-turbo)
   - `pass-6-observability-agent.md` (Target: openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-coder-v4)

2. Create `pipeline_v3.py` which upgrades the orchestrator to do the following:
   - Run all 8 passes sequentially: 0 (Design), 1 (Contracts), 2 (Tests), 3 (Core), 4 (Refactor), 5 (Security), 6 (Observability), 7 (Docs).
   - Keep the HITL pause after Pass 0.
   - AFTER Passes 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 completes successfully, use `subprocess` to run `git add <target_file>` and `git commit -m "chore(ai): completed Pass X"`.
   
3. Implement the "Self-Correction Loop" for Passes 3, 4, 5, and 6:
   - When running the local test command (e.g., `pytest`), if the exit code is non-zero, capture the `stdout`/`stderr`.
   - Automatically trigger the OpenCode CLI again, feeding it the error log and asking it to fix the file.
   - Max retries: 2. If it fails 3 times, abort the pipeline so the human can intervene.
</deliverables>

<execution_rules>
- Ensure the `subprocess` calls for Git do not crash if there are no changes to commit (e.g., if the Refactor agent decides the code is already optimal).
- Comment the Python script heavily so I can understand the state machine.
</execution_rules>

<content>
1: # The Enterprise Agentic Software Development Framework
2: **Building a deterministic, artifact-driven AI developer pipeline using OpenCode.**
3: 
4: _(While this architecture focuses on software development teams, it is easy to extended this to all employees by replacing IDEs with appropriate genAI clients and harnesses i.e. replace opencode+Bloop by [AnythingLLM](https://github.com/mintplex-labs/anything-llm) while retaining the LiteLLM and OpenRouter.)_
5: 
6: This document outlines the architectural blueprint for scaling AI coding agents across an enterprise. The architecture uses mature open-source tools to optmise and balance multiple common trade-offs in AI development. (The actual implementation will be opensourced soon.)
7: 
8: 
9: **Platform & Governance:** (Driven by LiteLLM, OpenRouter, Bloop, and Git Workflows)
10: - **Budget Control & Token Efficiency:** Granular token rationing and state-of-the-art code context retrieval using bloop.
11: - **Model Independence:** A proxy-first approach to avoid vendor lock-in (dynamically routing between Claude, DeepSeek, and OpenAI or models of your choice).
12: - **Enterprise-Grade Security & Auditing:** SSO Ready, PII masking, scoped access, and centralized AI telemetry.
13: - **Deterministic Execution:** Sandboxed agent environments to ensure reproducible builds.
14: - **Human Control:** Visual approval checkpoints and atomic Git commit workflows.
15: 
16: **Code Quality & Practices:** (Driven by 8-pass pipeline, TDD, Mermaid, opencode system prompts and Atomic Commits)
17: - **Output Accuracy:** Guaranteed via strict Test-Driven Development (TDD) constraints.
18: - **Zero Specification Drift:** Synchronizing executable specs (Mermaid/Gherkin) with core logic on every pass.
19: - **Readability & Traceability:** Automated dependency linking between code, tests, and architectural diagrams.
20: - **Observability:** Dedicated pipeline passes ensuring uniform error handling, logging, and telemetry.
21: - **Global Context Awareness:** Eliminating hallucinations via cross-repository semantic indexing.
22: 
23: By enforcing strict pipelines, localized context retrieval, and artifact-driven development, this framework eliminates context window bloat, prevents specification drift, and reduces LLM API costs significantly (needs further benchmarking) compared to ad-hoc agentic workflows.

62: 
63: ## 1. Background and Limitations
64: 
65: For the past two years, proprietary and open-source genAI coding tools have been evolving rapidly. They have been evolving faster than the developer community has been able to keep up. While the tools have been getting increasingly powerful and feature rich, it has been difficult to harness this power for teams. There are many public and celebrated "Agents.md" files but they focus only on the Agents and not the engineering around the Agents. There is also the FOMO factor on whether we are missing some capabilities or not by not using the very latest and greatest tools.
66: 
67: This unstructured approach fails at the enterprise level for three reasons:
68: 1. **Context Bloat:** Dumping massive files into an Agentic window burns millions of expensive tokens.
69: 2. **Spaghetti Edits:** Asking a single model to write core logic, implement security, and format logging simultaneously leads to "attention degradation". The model will inevitably "lazy code" one of these constraints.
70: 3. **Specification Drift:** The Agentic model changes the code, but the architectural documentation and requirements are left untouched, creating a legacy codebase on day one.
71: 
72: To solve this, we evolved the approach to agent development to: **AI as an Assembly Line.**
73: 
74: ### 1.1 The Proposed Paradigm: The Multi-Pass Pipeline
75: 
76: Instead of a single zero-shot prompt, development is broken down into a strict, sequential pipeline. Each step (pass) is handled by a specialized sub-agent with a deeply constrained scope and strict guard-rails.
77: 
78: > **The Decision:** We use a 8-pass pipeline (Design -> Contracts -> Tests -> Core Logic -> Refactor -> Security -> Observability -> Documentation).
79: >
80: > **The Rationale:** By strictly scoping each pass, we eliminate attention degradation. A "Security Agent" tasked *only* with finding OWASP vulnerabilities in a pre-written file performs significantly better than a generalist agent trying to write logic and secure it at the same time. Furthermore, tight scoping allows us to route simpler tasks to cheaper models, drastically reducing API costs.
81: 
82: ```mermaid
83: graph TD
84:     %% Consistent C4-inspired Style Definitions
85:     classDef orchestrator fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
86:     classDef subAgent fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
87:     classDef gate fill:#f59e0b,stroke:#b45309,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
88:     classDef external fill:#999999,stroke:#666666,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
89: 
90:     %% Nodes
91:     Orchestrator["Main Orchestrator <br> (Context & State Manager)"]:::orchestrator
92:     SubAgent["Specialized Sub-Agent <br> (e.g., Security, Observability)"]:::subAgent
93:     Gate{"Verification Gate <br> (Tests, Semgrep)"}:::gate
94:     Git[("Git Repository")]:::external
95: 
96:     %% Flow
97:     Orchestrator -->|1. Delegates scope & task boundaries| SubAgent
98:     
99:     SubAgent -->|2. Writes code / proposes diffs| Gate
100:     
101:     Gate -->|3. Fails: Feed error logs back| SubAgent
102:     
103:     Gate -->|4. Passes: Yield control back| Orchestrator
104:     
105:     Orchestrator -->|5. Commit atomic changes| Git
106:     Orchestrator -->|6. Trigger next pipeline pass| Orchestrator
107: ```
108: 
109: ### 1.2 Core Tenet: Artifact-Driven Development
110: 
111: In traditional development, documentation is a markdown file written after the fact. In an AI-Native pipeline, **the artifacts are the source of truth, and the code is merely a byproduct.** AWS Kiro does a great job here but it has some constraints around model selection and customizability.
112: 
113: We rely on two core artifacts:
114: *   **`.mmd` (Mermaid.js):** Text-based sequence, state, and class diagrams.
115: *   **`.gherkin` (Behavior-Driven Specs):** Executable Given/When/Then requirements.
116: 
117: > **The Decision:** No agent is allowed to write core logic until a Mermaid diagram and a Gherkin specification have been generated, updated, and approved by a human. This Human-in-the-loop is our check against AI hallucination.
118: >
119: > **The Rationale:** LLMs are prone to "logical tangents" when writing code directly. Forcing the AI to map a state machine in Mermaid.js *first* enforces Architectural Chain-of-Thought. When the AI subsequently writes the code, it uses its own diagram as a strict mathematical constraint, virtually eliminating logical hallucinations. Diagrams are easier for humans to understand and follow, making it easier to catch unhandled scenarios and edge cases, thus reducing the cognitive load on the developer. This also helps in maintaining backward compatibility and ease of onboarding new developers.
120: 
121: (*Link to Traceability Matrix Diagram in Appendix.*)
122: 
123: ### 1.3 Eliminating Specification Drift
124: 
125: The greatest risk of agentic coding (apart from the obvious hallucinations and questionable human oversight) is the speed at which it can outpace its own documentation.
126: 
127: > **The Decision:** We treat architectural diagrams and Gherkin specs as version-controlled, executable code. The pipeline enforces a mandatory "Artifact Sync" rule: an agent mandatorily updates the '.mmd' and '.gherkin' and takes human approval of these changes before touching any core logic. 
128: >
129: > **The Rationale:** This creates a "Digital Twin" of your software. By utilizing `JSDoc @see` links pointing directly to local `.mmd` files, human developers can instantly trace complex AI-generated code back to the exact state transition diagram that dictated it. Spec drift becomes impossible because the spec and the code are locked in a continuous feedback loop.
130: 
131: ```mermaid
132: graph TD
133:     %% Consistent C4 Style Definitions
134:     classDef actor fill:#08427b,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff,rx:20,ry:20
135:     classDef coreSystem fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
136:     classDef internalComp fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
137:     classDef extSystem fill:#999999,stroke:#666666,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
138:     
139:     %% Phase Styling
140:     classDef phaseRed fill:#fee2e2,stroke:#b91c1c,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
141:     classDef phaseGreen fill:#dcfce7,stroke:#15803d,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
142:     classDef phaseRefactor fill:#fef3c7,stroke:#b45309,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
143: 
144:     %% Actors and Inputs
145:     Dev(["Developer / Product Manager"]):::actor
146:     Ticket["New Feature Request <br> (Modifies Existing Module)"]:::extSystem
147:     Bloop[("Bloop Indexer <br> (Retrieves Existing Specs)")]:::internalComp
148: 
149:     subgraph DesignPhase ["1. Spec Evolution (Pass 0)"]
150:         direction TB
151:         UpdateMMD["Agent updates existing design.mmd"]:::coreSystem
152:         UpdateGherkin["Agent updates existing spec.gherkin"]:::coreSystem
153:         HITL{"Human Approval <br> (Reviews Architecture Diff)"}:::actor
154:     end
155: 
156:     subgraph TDDPhase ["2. Test Evolution (Pass 2)"]
157:         direction TB
158:         WriteTests["Agent updates test_suite.ts <br> to match new specs"]:::phaseRed
159:         RunFail["Run Tests: FAIL <br> (Ensures tests are valid constraints)"]:::phaseRed
160:     end
161: 
162:     subgraph CodePhase ["3. Code Evolution (Pass 3)"]
163:         direction TB
164:         UpdateCode["Agent edits implementation.ts"]:::phaseGreen
165:         RunPass["Run Tests: PASS <br> (Code meets new specs)"]:::phaseGreen
166:     end
167: 
168:     subgraph CIPhase ["4. Hardening (Pass 4-7 - REFACTOR)"]
169:         direction TB
170:         Pipeline["Refactor, Security, Logging <br> (Tests run continuously)"]:::phaseRefactor
171:         FinalSync["Pass 7 Docs: Verify Specs <br> match final code"]:::phaseRefactor
172:     end
173: 
174:     %% Flow Relationships
175:     Dev --> Ticket
176:     Ticket --> UpdateMMD
177:     Bloop -. "Provides existing context" .-> UpdateMMD
178:     
179:     UpdateMMD --> UpdateGherkin
180:     UpdateGherkin --> HITL
181:     
182:     HITL -- "Approved" --> WriteTests
183:     HITL -. "Rejected" .-> UpdateMMD
184:     
185:     WriteTests --> RunFail
186:     RunFail -- "Triggers Implementation" --> UpdateCode
187:     
188:     UpdateCode --> RunPass
189:     
190:     RunPass -- "Commits to CI" --> Pipeline
191:     Pipeline --> FinalSync
192: ```
193: 
194: **The Reality Check: Why Diagrams Actually Reduce Costs**
195: 
196: The "Multi-Pass Pipeline" sounds expensive: multiple API calls, multiple context windows, human approval gates.
197: 
198: However, in practice, this system acts as a **Context Collapse Filter**. Consider the alternative: a "Zero-Shot" approach where a single agent writes the code directly from the initial ticket.
199: 
200: Without a visual constraint, the agent must hold the entire feature logic, plus the entirety of the existing codebase (e.g., the `Order` module), in its context window simultaneously. This inevitably leads to **Logical Dilution**, where the agent "lazy codes" constraints to save token space, resulting in bugs that require hours of debugging.
201: 
202: By forcing the creation of a Mermaid diagram first, we do the following:
203: 1. **Token Compression:** A Mermaid diagram encoding 500 lines of logic uses 90% fewer tokens than the source code itself.
204: 2. **Early Error Detection:** A human can spot a logical flaw in a 200-token diagram in seconds, preventing a 2,000-line buggy implementation that would take hours to refactor.
205: 3. **Recursive Constraint:** The diagram becomes a persistent, cheap "Context Anchor" that can be re-fed to the agent in subsequent passes without blowing the budget.
206: 
207: ---
208: 
209: ## 2. The Architecture & Infrastructure
210: 
211: To execute an 8-pass agentic pipeline safely across hundreds of developers, the underlying infrastructure must enforce security, budget constraints, and context accuracy before a single prompt reaches an LLM. 
212: 
213: We achieve this by decoupling the agent from the LLM provider, utilizing a secure gateway proxy, and building a centralized semantic knowledge graph.
214: 
215: ### 2.1 The Model Gateway: LiteLLM + OpenRouter + SSO
216: 
217: Relying on a single vendor (like GitHub Copilot or ChatGPT Enterprise) locks an organization into arbitrary pricing models, limits model choice, and removes granular auditing capabilities.
218: 
219: > **The Decision:** We route all agent traffic through a self-hosted [**LiteLLM**](https://github.com/BerriAI/litellm) (or [Bifrost](https://github.com/maximhq/bifrost)) proxy, authenticated via corporate SSO (O365/GSuite), which then multiplexes requests to **OpenRouter** (or internal models).
220: >
221: > **The Rationale:** 
222: > *   **Budget Rationing:** LiteLLM intercepts the SSO identity and checks it against the internal Postgres database. We can enforce hard monthly budgets per developer or per department. Once the budget is hit, the proxy returns a `402 Payment Required`, preventing runaway agent loops from causing massive API bills. (Optionally, We can also have a fallback option of cheaper/smaller models with some warning.)
223: > *   **Model Routing:** Pass 1 (Contracts) requires the strict formatting of Claude 3.7 (or higher), while Pass 3 (Core Logic) can be handled by the 80% cheaper DeepSeek v4 (or other models). The proxy allows us to dynamically route tasks to the most cost-effective model without changing the developer's local tools.
224: > *   **PII & Data Loss Prevention (DLP):** The proxy acts as a firewall. Middleware can strip sensitive API keys, DB credentials, or PII from the prompt before it ever leaves the corporate network.
225: 
226: ```mermaid
227: graph LR
228:     %% Consistent Style Definitions
229:     classDef actor fill:#08427b,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff,rx:20,ry:20
230:     classDef coreSystem fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
231:     classDef internalComp fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
232:     classDef extSystem fill:#999999,stroke:#666666,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
233: 
234:     %% Nodes
235:     Dev(["Developer IDE"]):::actor
236: 
237:     subgraph Proxy ["Internal AI Gateway (LiteLLM)"]
238:         direction LR
239:         Auth["1. Identity Check <br> (SSO/OIDC)"]:::coreSystem
240:         Quota["2. Budget Gate <br> (Quota Check)"]:::internalComp
241:         DLP["3. Privacy Filter <br> (DLP Masking)"]:::internalComp
242:     end
243: 
244:     Target["OpenRouter API <br> (External LLMs)"]:::extSystem
245: 
246:     %% Execution Flow
247:     Dev ==> Auth
248:     Auth ==> Quota
249:     Quota ==> DLP
250:     DLP ==> Target
251: 
252:     %% Simple Legend/Status
253:     Target -. "Response & Token Billing" .-> Proxy
254: ```
255: A more detailed diagram can be found in the Appendix (**Placeholder for link to Diagram**)
256: 
257: ### 2.2 The Knowledge Layer: Bloop AI & Semantic Indexing
258: 
259: An AI agent is only as intelligent as the context it is given. Under-optimised agentic tools (including Gemini-cli, Claude-Code) attempt to solve this by context stuffing or inefficiently running `grep` across the terminal or asking the user to drag-and-drop files, which leads to massive token waste and missed cross-repository dependencies.
260: 
261: > **The Decision:** We deploy [**Bloop AI**](https://github.com/BloopAI/bloop) (or a similar vector/AST indexer like Zoekt) as an internal service to index all Git repositories, acting as the semantic search engine for the OpenCode orchestrator.
262: >
263: > **The Rationale:** When a developer asks an agent to "update the payment retry logic," the Pass 0 (Design) agent queries the Bloop API. Bloop returns the exact `.mmd` diagrams, TypeScript interfaces, and database schemas required from across multiple microservices. This surgically precise context window (hundreds of tokens instead of thousands) prevents hallucinations and ensures the agent adheres to existing architectural patterns.
264: 
265: ```mermaid
266: graph LR
267:     %% Consistent Style Definitions
268:     classDef actor fill:#08427b,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff,rx:20,ry:20
269:     classDef coreSystem fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
270:     classDef internalComp fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px,color:#000
271:     classDef extSystem fill:#999999,stroke:#666666,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
272: 
273:     %% Nodes
274:     Repos["Internal Repos <br> (GitHub/GitLab)"]:::extSystem
275:     
276:     subgraph "Background: Indexing"
277:         direction TB
278:         Bloop["Bloop Engine <br> (Parser & Indexer)"]:::coreSystem
279:         DB[("Search & Vector DB <br> (The Knowledge)")]:::internalComp
280:     end
281: 
282:     subgraph "Foreground: Retrieval"
283:         direction TB
284:         Agent["OpenCode Agent <br> (The Orchestrator)"]:::coreSystem
285:     end
286: 
287:     %% Data Flow
288:     Repos -- "Sync Code" --> Bloop
289:     Bloop -- "Create Graph" --> DB
290:     
291:     Agent -- "Ask: 'Where is...?'" --> DB
292:     DB -- "Return Exact Code" --> Agent
293: 
294:     %% Labels
295:     style DB fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e
296: ```
297: (Placeholder: Insert Link to detailed "Retrieval/Indexing Architecture Diagram" here)
298: 
299: ### 2.3 Deterministic Environments (The Agent Sandbox)
300: 
301: Because our pipeline relies on a strict TDD methodology (Pass 2 tests *must* fail before Pass 3 writes code), the agents must be able to execute terminal commands like `npm test`, `mvn clean install`, or `pytest`. 
302: 
303: > **The Decision:** Agent execution is strictly bound to deterministic, containerized environments using **DevContainers (`devcontainer.json`)** or **Nix flakes**. (Implementation pending.)
304: >
305: > **The Rationale:** If an agent runs a test on a developer's local machine that has the wrong Node.js version, the test will fail due to environment errors. The agent will then hallucinate, attempting to rewrite perfectly good code to "fix" a problem that is actually an environment mismatch. By forcing agents to run in a sandboxed container, we guarantee reproducible builds, protect the host machine from rogue agent scripts, and ensure the TDD loop is cryptographically reliable.
306: 
307: ---
308: 
309: ## 3. The 8-Pass Pipeline & Model Strategy
310: 
311: The heart of the our OpenCode Enterprise Framework is the orchestrator script that transitions the agent through eight strictly scoped phases. By decomposing the software development lifecycle (SDLC) into granular agentic tasks, we can apply the "Actor-Critic" and "Red-Green-Refactor" methodologies programmatically.
312: 
313: ```mermaid
314: ---
315: title: 7-Pass Agentic TDD Pipeline (State Machine)
316: ---
317: stateDiagram-v2
318:     %% Consistent Styling Definitions
319:     classDef human fill:#08427b,color:#fff,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px
320:     classDef agent fill:#1168bd,color:#fff,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px
321:     classDef testGate fill:#2dd4bf,color:#000,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px
322: 
323:     [*] --> Pass_0
324:     
325:     %% --- PHASE 1: Design & Specs ---
326:     Pass_0 : Pass 0 - Design & Context (Agent)
327:     class Pass_0 agent
328:     
329:     HITL : Developer Review (HITL)
330:     class HITL human
331:     
332:     Pass_0 --> HITL : Outputs .mmd & .gherkin
333:     HITL --> Pass_0 : Request Architecture Changes
334:     HITL --> Pass_1 : Approve Specs
335:     
336:     %% --- PHASE 2: Contracts & Tests ---
337:     Pass_1 : Pass 1 - Contracts & Types (Agent)
338:     class Pass_1 agent
339:     
340:     Pass_2 : Pass 2 - Test Generation [Red Phase]
341:     class Pass_2 agent
342:     
343:     Pass_1 --> Pass_2
344:     Pass_2 --> Pass_3
345:     
346:     %% --- PHASE 3: Core Implementation ---
347:     Pass_3 : Pass 3 - Core Logic [Green Phase]
348:     class Pass_3 agent
349:     
350:     Gate_3 : Test Runner (Verify Core)
351:     class Gate_3 testGate
352:     
353:     Pass_3 --> Gate_3
354:     Gate_3 --> Pass_3 : Tests Failed (Fix Core)
355:     Gate_3 --> Pass_4 : Tests Passed
356:     
357:     %% --- PHASE 4: Refactor ---
358:     Pass_4 : Pass 4 - Clean Code & Refactor
359:     class Pass_4 agent
360:     
361:     Gate_4 : Test Runner (Verify Refactor)
362:     class Gate_4 testGate
363: 
364:     Pass_4 --> Gate_4
365:     Gate_4 --> Pass_4 : Refactor Broke Logic (Revert & Fix)
366:     Gate_4 --> Pass_5 : Tests Passed
367:     
368:     %% --- PHASE 5: Security ---
369:     Pass_5 : Pass 5 - Security Hardening
370:     class Pass_5 agent
371:     
372:     Gate_5 : Test Runner (Verify Security)
373:     class Gate_5 testGate
374:     
375:     Pass_5 --> Gate_5
376:     Gate_5 --> Pass_5 : Security Blocked Valid Logic (Fix)
377:     Gate_5 --> Pass_6 : Tests Passed
378:     
379:     %% --- PHASE 6: Observability ---
380:     Pass_6 : Pass 6 - Observability & Logs
381:     class Pass_6 agent
382:     
383:     Gate_6 : Test Runner (Verify Observability)
384:     class Gate_6 testGate
385:     
386:     Pass_6 --> Gate_6
387:     Gate_6 --> Pass_6 : Logs Broke Scopes/Types (Fix)
388:     Gate_6 --> Pass_7 : Tests Passed
389:     
390:     %% --- PHASE 7: Documentation & Spec Sync ---
391:     Pass_7 : Pass 7 - Sync Docs & Spec Artifacts
392:     class Pass_7 agent
393:     
394:     Gate_7 : Final CI/CD Verification
395:     class Gate_7 testGate
396:     
397:     Pass_7 --> Gate_7
398:     Gate_7 --> Pass_7 : Spec Drift Detected (Update Specs)
399:     Gate_7 --> [*] : Branch Ready for PR
400: ```
401: 
402: ### 3.1 The Pipeline Breakdown
403: 
404: The workflow requires the OpenCode orchestrator to sequentially trigger the following sub-agents:
405: 
406: 1. **Pass 0: Design & Context** (The Architect)
407:    * *Goal:* Read the feature ticket, query Bloop for repository context, and generate/update the `design.mmd` (Mermaid diagrams) and `spec.gherkin`. 
408:    * *Gate:* Requires human (Developer) approval before proceeding.
409: 2. **Pass 1: Contracts & Interfaces** (The Modeler)
410:    * *Goal:* Define the strict API boundaries, types, and data schemas (e.g., TypeScript Interfaces, Pydantic models).
411: 3. **Pass 2: TDD Test Generation** (The QA Red Phase)
412:    * *Goal:* Write comprehensive unit and edge-case tests against the Pass 1 interfaces based purely on the Pass 0 diagrams. Do *not* write core logic.
413: 4. **Pass 3: Core Implementation** (The Builder Green Phase)
414:    * *Goal:* Write the algorithmic logic to make the Pass 2 tests pass. 
415:    * *Gate:* `npm test` must pass. If it fails, the agent reads the error log and self-corrects.
416: 5. **Pass 4: Refactor & Optimization** (The Optimizer)
417:    * *Goal:* Reduce cyclomatic complexity, enforce DRY principles, and optimize Big-O performance without changing behavior.
418:    * *Gate:* `npm test` must pass to ensure the refactor didn't break functionality.
419: 6. **Pass 5: Security Hardening** (The Red Team)
420:    * *Goal:* Add input sanitization, OWASP mitigations, and boundary validation (e.g., Zod schemas). 
421:    * *Gate:* `npm test` must pass.
422: 7. **Pass 6: Observability** (The SRE)
423:    * *Goal:* Implement uniform try/catch blocks, structured JSON logging, and custom error classes.
424:    * *Gate:* `npm test` must pass.
425: 8. **Pass 7: Documentation** (The Tech Writer)
426:    * *Goal:* Generate JSDoc/Docstrings, sync the Traceability Matrix, and ensure the README and inline comments reflect the final implementation.
427: 
428: ### 3.2 Dynamic Model Routing (The OpenRouter Strategy)
429: 
430: Using a frontier model (like Claude 4.x Sonnet or GPT-4.5) for all eight passes is financially irresponsible at an enterprise scale. Because we use LiteLLM and OpenRouter, we lock specific models to specific passes based on their training strengths.
431: 
432: > **The Decision:** We route Architectural passes to **Claude**, Logic/Execution passes to **DeepSeek**, Security passes to **OpenAI**, and text generation to **Llama/Gemini**. 
433: > 
434: >*(Given the bloop integration and resultant high-quality context, we think that 30B-300B param models too might do a great (or at least adequate) job for exeution passes 3-4 and 6,7. You should probably use a frontier model for the Security pass (pass 5) though.). Some more experiments with different models for different passes will be very helful.*
435: >
436: > **The Rationale:** 
437: > *   **Claude 3.7 Sonnet or higher (Passes 0 & 1):** Claude is the industry leader in Constitutional Adherence and Systems Design. It excels at reading messy Jira tickets and translating them into flawless XML and Mermaid.js boundaries without hallucinating premature code.
438: > *   **DeepSeek v4 (Passes 2, 3, & 4):** DeepSeek is an algorithmic powerhouse. For pure "make the tests pass" mathematical logic, it matches or beats proprietary frontier models at roughly 10% of the cost. It is our heavy-lifting engine.
439: > *   **GPT-4.5 (Pass 5 - Security):** OpenAI models undergo massive corporate RLHF (Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback) for defensive cybersecurity. We pay the premium token cost here to leverage its deep red-teaming mindset to spot injection flaws.
440: > *   **Llama 3 70B / Gemini 2.5 Flash (Passes 6 & 7):** Adding logging and writing docstrings is highly repetitive, mundane prose. We route this to blazing-fast, nearly-free models to minimize overhead.
441: 
442: ### 3.3 Execution: Atomic Commits vs. Bulk Edits
443: 
444: In a multi-pass system running locally, the compute overhead of testing is negligible, but the risk of "merge hell" is high.
445: 
446: > **The Decision:** The pipeline is orchestrated to pause, run the test suite, and execute an atomic `git commit` after *every individual pass* (starting from Pass 1), rather than squashing all AI edits into a single feature commit.
447: > *Example:* `git commit -m "chore(ai): applied security hardening"`
448: >
449: > **The Rationale:** If an agent outputs a massive single commit containing core logic, security updates, and new logs, and the application subsequently crashes, the developer has no idea which sub-agent broke the code. By testing and committing sequentially, a developer can pinpoint exactly which pass caused the regression and surgically `git revert` just that step, adjust the `agents.xml` prompt, and retry. This turns debugging an AI hallucination from a multi-hour headache into a 30-second revert.
450: 
451: ---
452: 
453: ## 4. Agent Guardrails & Prompt Engineering
454: 
455: Giving autonomous agents write-access to your codebase and API keys introduces massive risk. Without strict guardrails, an agent might accidentally overwrite business logic while trying to add a log statement, or fall victim to a "Prompt Injection" attack hidden in a legacy code comment.
456: 
457: To mitigate this, we define the agents' personas, constraints, and instructions using strict structural formatting within a centralized `.opencode/` directory in every repository.
458: 
459: ### 4.1 XML Prompting over Markdown
460: 
461: Most agentic systems use Markdown (`# Instructions`, `## Context`) to prompt the LLM. For complex, multi-agent pipelines, Markdown is fundamentally flawed because it lacks strict boundaries. 
462: 
463: > **The Decision:** All sub-agent personas and system instructions must be formatted using strict XML tags (e.g., `<system_instructions>`, `<user_code>`, `<action_plan>`) rather than Markdown headers.
464: >
465: > **The Rationale:** If you use Markdown and feed the AI a codebase file that *also* contains Markdown comments, the LLM can easily confuse the code's comments for pipeline instructions (Prompt Injection). XML creates absolute semantic walls. The LLM understands that everything inside `<user_code> ... </user_code>` is purely a payload to be analyzed, not a command to be executed. This is Anthropic's recommended standard for zero-hallucination agent routing.
466: 
467: *Example of a secure `.opencode/agents.xml` definition:*
468: ```xml
469: <agent>
470:   <role>Security Hardening Agent</role>
471:   <directives>
472:     <rule>Find and mitigate OWASP vulnerabilities.</rule>
473:     <rule>Do NOT modify the core algorithmic logic.</rule>
474:   </directives>
475:   <context>
476:     <!-- Injected by Bloop Retrieval -->
477:     {{COMPANY_SECURITY_PATTERNS}}
478:   </context>
479:   <task>
480:     Review the payload in the user_code tag. Output proposed fixes as Diffs.
481:   </task>
482: </agent>
483: ```
484: 
485: ### 4.2 Agent Isolation and Scope Locking
486: 
487: If the Observability Agent (Pass 6) decides that the core logic is "messy" and rewrites it while adding logs, the pipeline breaks. We must enforce the "Separation of Concerns" at the file and Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) level.
488: 
489: > **The Decision:** Agents are heavily restricted via "Scope Guardrails." If an agent believes an out-of-scope change is required (e.g., the Docs Agent realizes the Core Logic is flawed), it is forbidden from making the change. It must pause, delegate a request back to the Orchestrator, and wait for human intervention.
490: >
491: > **The Rationale:** This prevents "Agent Trampling." By enforcing strict write-locks based on the pipeline phase (e.g., Pass 2 can only write to `*.spec.ts`, Pass 7 can only edit comments/docstrings), we guarantee that downstream passes do not silently undo the verified work of upstream passes. 
492: 
493: ### 4.3 Automated Hard-Fail Gates (Semgrep)
494: 
495: Even with the best models, we cannot trust AI-generated code blindly, especially concerning security and internal compliance.
496: 
497: > **The Decision:** The pipeline incorporates static analysis tools like **Semgrep** as automated "Hard-Fail" gates between passes.
498: >
499: > **The Rationale:** If the DeepSeek Core Logic agent (Pass 3) writes a working feature, but includes a hardcoded secret or a SQL injection vulnerability, Semgrep intercepts the code during the verification gate. Instead of passing the vulnerable code to the human, the pipeline automatically feeds the Semgrep error trace back to the agent for self-correction. The human never sees the code until it passes all deterministic static analysis checks.
500: 
501: ---
502: 
503: ## Next Steps and The Path Forward
504: 
505: By implementing the **Nistapp-OpenCode Enterprise Framework**, organizations stop paying for bloated token context windows and stop suffering from specification drift. Instead, developers become **System Orchestrators**—curating architecture via Mermaid diagrams, defining executable Gherkin specs, and reviewing atomic, verified Git commits generated by a highly disciplined, multi-pass AI pipeline.
506: 
507: This is a significant step towards a fundamentally safer, more maintainable way to build enterprise software.

609: > 3. Pipeline Lifecycle
610: ```mermaid
611: stateDiagram
612:     %% Consistent Styling Definitions
613:     classDef state fill:#1168bd,color:#fff,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px
614:     classDef gate fill:#2dd4bf,color:#000,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px
615:     classDef human fill:#08427b,color:#fff,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px
616:     classDef endState fill:#999999,color:#fff,stroke:#666666,stroke-width:2px
617: 
618:     [*] --> Feature_Request
619:     class Feature_Request human
620: 
621:     Feature_Request --> Design_Phase : Assign to Pass 0
622: 
623:     %% Phase 1: The Design Contract
624:     state Design_Phase {
625:         [*] --> Draft_Artifacts : Generate .mmd & .gherkin
626:         Draft_Artifacts --> Human_Review : Propose Architecture
627:         
628:         Human_Review --> Draft_Artifacts : Reject (Modify Specs)
629:         Human_Review --> [*] : Approve Design
630:     }
631:     class Design_Phase state
632:     class Human_Review human
633: 
634:     Design_Phase --> Implementation_Phase : Specs Locked
635:     
636:     %% Phase 2: The Agentic Code Factory
637:     state Implementation_Phase {
638:         [*] --> Write_Code : Passes 1-3 (Core)
639:         
640:         Write_Code --> Run_Tests : Execute TDD Suite
641:         Run_Tests --> Write_Code : Tests Failed (Retry)
642:         
643:         Run_Tests --> Sync_Artifacts : Tests Passed
644:         Sync_Artifacts --> Write_Code : Drift Detected (Loop)
645:         
646:         Sync_Artifacts --> [*] : Passes 4-7 Complete
647:     }
648:     class Implementation_Phase state
649: 
650:     Implementation_Phase --> Quality_Gate : Trigger CI/CD Guardrails
651:     class Quality_Gate gate
652: 
653:     %% Final Resolution
654:     Quality_Gate --> Implementation_Phase : Security / Linting Fail
655:     Quality_Gate --> PR_Merged : LGTM / PR Approved
656:     
657:     PR_Merged --> [*] : Production Ready
658:     class PR_Merged endState
659: ```

704:     %% Consistent C4-inspired Style Definitions
705:     classDef actor fill:#08427b,stroke:#052e56,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
706:     classDef coreSystem fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff

728:     Indexer -->|"2. Create Embeddings"| Qdrant
729:     Indexer -->|"3. Build AST/Trigrams"| Tantivy

733:     BloopAPI -->|"B. Query Context Meaning"| Qdrant
734:     BloopAPI -->|"C. Query Exact Symbols"| Tantivy
735:

737:     BloopAPI -.->|"D. Return High-Density Context"| Agent
738: ```

741: > 6. Knowledge Context Construction Flow
742: ```mermaid
743: graph TD
744:     %% Consistent C4-inspired Style Definitions
745:     classDef orchestrator fill:#1168bd,stroke:#0b4884,stroke-width:2px,color:#fff
746:     classDef knowledge fill:#2dd4bf,stroke:#0f766e,stroke-width:2px,color:#000

751: 
752:     %% Grouping the data sources logically
753:     subgraph Knowledge_Sources ["The Three Pillars of Context"]
754:         direction LR
755:         LocalDB[("Local Directory <br> (.opencode/patterns)")]:::knowledge
756:         BloopDB[("Global Context <br> (Bloop REST API)")]:::knowledge
757:         GitDB[("Local Git History <br> (Commit Logs & Diffs)")]:::knowledge
758:     end
759: 
760:     Pruner{"Context Merger & <br> Dynamic Pruning Layer"}:::action
761:     FinalPrompt["Optimized Prompt Payload <br> (XML-Wrapped)"]:::orchestrator
762:     LLM["Target LLM via OpenRouter <br> (DeepSeek / Claude)"]:::extSystem
763: 
764:     %% Step 1-3: Gathering Information
765:     Agent -->|"1. Query Architectural Rules"| LocalDB
766:     Agent -->|"2. Query Cross-Repo Types"| BloopDB
767:     Agent -->|"3. Query Intent & Changes"| GitDB
768: 
769:     %% Returning data to the Pruner
770:     LocalDB -.->|"Raw Rules"| Pruner
771:     BloopDB -.->|"Raw Dependencies"| Pruner
772:     GitDB -.->|"Raw Diffs"| Pruner
773: 
774:     %% Final Execution
775:     Pruner -->|"4. Trim, Deduplicate & Format"| FinalPrompt
776:     FinalPrompt -->|"5. Send Executable Prompt"| LLM
777: ```

779: ---
780: 7. Auth and Budgeting
781: ```mermaid
782: sequenceDiagram
783:     autonumber
784: 
785:     box rgb(240, 248, 255) "Internal Corporate Network"
786:         participant Dev as Developer IDE (OpenCode)
787:         participant Proxy as LiteLLM Proxy
788:         participant DB as Auth & Usage DB
789:     end
790: 
791:     box rgb(245, 245, 245) "Public Internet"
792:         participant OR as OpenRouter API
793:     end
794: 
795:     %% Initial Request
796:     Dev->>+Proxy: Request Model Completion (Auth Header)
797:     
798:     %% Identity Verification
799:     Note right of Proxy: OIDC Auth & Role Mapping
800:     Proxy->>+DB: Validate SSO Token
801:     DB-->>-Proxy: Identity Confirmed (User / Dept)
802:     
803:     %% Budgeting Gate
804:     Proxy->>+DB: Check Department/User Token Quota
805:     
806:     alt Quota Exceeded
807:         DB-->>Proxy: Status: Budget Exhausted
808:         Proxy-->>Dev: 402 Error: Department Quota Reached
809:     else Quota Available
810:         DB-->>-Proxy: Status: Budget Approved
811:         
812:         %% Security & Gateway Logic
813:         Note right of Proxy: Data Loss Prevention (DLP)<br/>Strip PII & Hardcoded Secrets
814:         Proxy->>+OR: Forward Sanitized Prompt
815:         
816:         %% Response & Accounting
817:         OR-->>-Proxy: Stream LLM Response
818:         
819:         Proxy->>+DB: Log Token Usage (Increment Counter)
820:         DB-->>-Proxy: Usage Updated
821:         
822:         Proxy-->>-Dev: Return Response to Developer
823:     end
824: ```
825:

<content>
1: #!/usr/bin/env python3
2: """
3: pipeline_v2.py — v0.2 AI Factory Pipeline Orchestrator
4: =======================================================
5: 
6: Executes a four-pass AI-native development pipeline against a single
7: target source file, using OpenCode CLI as the agent runner.
8: 
9: Pipeline passes
10: ---------------
11:   Pass 0  Design & Architecture  (Claude Sonnet 4.5)
12:           → Produces design.mmd + spec.gherkin
13:           → Human-in-the-Loop gate before any code is written
14: 
15:   Pass 1  Test Generation        (DeepSeek v4-pro)   [Red Phase]
16:           → Writes a test file derived from the Gherkin scenarios
17: 
18:   Pass 2  Core Implementation    (DeepSeek v4-pro)   [Green Phase]
19:           → Writes/improves source logic to satisfy Pass 1 tests
20:           → Verification gate: runs the local test suite via subprocess
21: 
22:   Pass 3  Documentation          (DeepSeek v4-pro)
23:           → Adds JSDoc / Python docstrings (no logic changes)
24: 
25: Usage
26: -----
27:   python pipeline_v2.py <target_file> [options]
28: 
29:   python pipeline_v2.py src/calculator.py
30:   python pipeline_v2.py src/calculator.py --test-cmd "pytest src/ -k calculator -v"
31:   python pipeline_v2.py src/calculator.py --skip-hitl   # CI / automated use
32: 
33: Prerequisites
34: -------------
35:   - opencode CLI on $PATH  (npm install -g opencode-ai)
36:   - OPENROUTER_API_KEY in .env or already exported to the shell
37:   - Agent files present in .opencode/agent/
38: """
39: 
40: import argparse
41: import os
42: import shlex
43: import shutil
44: import subprocess
45: import sys
46: from pathlib import Path
47: 
48: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
49: # Constants
50: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
51: 
52: PIPELINE_VERSION = "0.2"
53: 
54: # opencode CLI binary name — must be on $PATH
55: OPENCODE_CMD = "opencode"
56: 
57: # Maps logical pass names to agent IDs.
58: # Agent IDs must match filenames under .opencode/agent/<id>.md
59: AGENTS = {
60:     "design":     "pass-0-design-agent",
61:     "tests":      "test-generation-agent",
62:     "implement":  "core-implementation-agent",
63:     "docs":       "documentation-agent",
64: }
65: 
66: # Width for decorative box-drawing in terminal output
67: _W = 64
68: 
69: 
70: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
71: # Environment helpers
72: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
73: 
74: def load_dot_env(env_path: Path = Path(".env")) -> None:
75:     """Parse a .env file and populate os.environ.
76: 
77:     Variables already present in the environment take precedence
78:     (shell-level overrides are not clobbered).  Blank lines and lines
79:     starting with '#' are silently skipped.  Inline comments (# …) and
80:     surrounding quotes on values are stripped.
81: 
82:     Args:
83:         env_path: Path to the .env file.  Defaults to ./.env
84:     """
85:     if not env_path.is_file():
86:         return
87: 
88:     with env_path.open() as fh:
89:         for raw in fh:
90:             line = raw.strip()
91: 
92:             # Skip blank lines and comments
93:             if not line or line.startswith("#") or "=" not in line:
94:                 continue
95: 
96:             key, _, raw_value = line.partition("=")
97: 
98:             # Strip inline comment, then surrounding quotes
99:             clean_value = raw_value.split("#")[0].strip().strip("'\"")
100: 
101:             # setdefault: shell env overrides .env
102:             os.environ.setdefault(key.strip(), clean_value)
103: 
104: 
105: def preflight_checks(target: Path) -> None:
106:     """Validate all prerequisites before any pipeline pass runs.
107: 
108:     Aborts with a descriptive error message if any check fails,
109:     preventing a partially-run pipeline with misleading side-effects.
110: 
111:     Args:
112:         target: Resolved path to the target source file.
113: 
114:     Raises:
115:         SystemExit(1): On any failed check.
116:     """
117:     if not target.is_file():
118:         _die(f"Target file not found: '{target}'")
119: 
120:     if not os.environ.get("OPENROUTER_API_KEY"):
121:         _die(
122:             "OPENROUTER_API_KEY is not set.\n"
123:             "  Add it to your .env file:  OPENROUTER_API_KEY=sk-or-..."
124:         )
125: 
126:     if not shutil.which(OPENCODE_CMD):
127:         _die(
128:             f"'{OPENCODE_CMD}' CLI not found on PATH.\n"
129:             "  Install it with:  npm install -g opencode-ai"
130:         )
131: 
132: 
133: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
134: # Terminal output helpers
135: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
136: 
137: def _banner(target: Path, test_cmd: list[str], skip_hitl: bool) -> None:
138:     """Print the pipeline startup banner."""
139:     print()
140:     print("┌" + "─" * _W + "┐")
141:     print(f"│  ai-factory-setup  •  v{PIPELINE_VERSION} Pipeline" + " " * (_W - 33) + "│")
142:     print("└" + "─" * _W + "┘")
143:     print()
144:     print(f"  Target     : {target}")
145:     print(f"  Test cmd   : {' '.join(test_cmd)}")
146:     print(f"  HITL gate  : {'disabled (--skip-hitl)' if skip_hitl else 'enabled'}")
147:     print()
148: 
149: 
150: def _pass_header(label: str) -> None:
151:     """Print a visually distinct header for each pipeline pass."""
152:     print()
153:     print("━" * _W)
154:     print(f"  {label}")
155:     print("━" * _W)
156:     print()
157: 
158: 
159: def _pass_ok(label: str) -> None:
160:     """Print a pass-completion confirmation."""
161:     print(f"\n  ✓  {label} — complete.\n")
162: 
163: 
164: def _warn(lines: list[str]) -> None:
165:     """Print a loud, boxed warning block that does NOT abort the pipeline.
166: 
167:     Args:
168:         lines: Individual lines of the warning message body.
169:     """
170:     print()
171:     print("┌" + "─" * _W + "┐")
172:     print("│  ⚠  WARNING" + " " * (_W - 12) + "│")
173:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
174:     for line in lines:
175:         padded = f"│  {line}"
176:         print(padded + " " * max(0, _W + 1 - len(padded)) + "│")
177:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
178:     print("└" + "─" * _W + "┘")
179:     print()
180: 
181: 
182: def _die(msg: str) -> None:
183:     """Print a fatal error message and exit with code 1.
184: 
185:     Args:
186:         msg: Error description.  May contain newlines for multiline output.
187:     """
188:     print(f"\n[ERROR]  {msg}\n", file=sys.stderr)
189:     sys.exit(1)
190: 
191: 
192: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
193: # OpenCode runner
194: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
195: 
196: def run_opencode(
197:     agent: str,
198:     prompt: str,
199:     files: list[Path],
200: ) -> None:
201:     """Invoke `opencode run` for a single pipeline pass.
202: 
203:     Streams all output directly to the terminal so the developer sees
204:     live diffs and agent reasoning as they happen.  The model is NOT
205:     specified here — each agent's frontmatter owns its model declaration.
206:     This keeps model selection co-located with agent definitions and
207:     ensures `agents.xml` remains the single source of truth.
208: 
209:     Args:
210:         agent:  Agent ID matching .opencode/agent/<agent>.md
211:         prompt: The user-turn message sent to the agent.
212:         files:  Source files to attach to the message via repeated --file flags.
213: 
214:     Raises:
215:         subprocess.CalledProcessError: If opencode exits with a non-zero code.
216:         KeyboardInterrupt: Propagated as-is; handled by the caller.
217:     """
218:     cmd = [OPENCODE_CMD, "run", "--agent", agent]
219: 
220:     # Attach every file with its own --file flag (opencode supports repeats)
221:     for f in files:
222:         cmd += ["--file", str(f)]
223: 
224:     # Auto-approve permissions that aren't explicitly denied in the agent's
225:     # frontmatter.  Safe here because all agents deny bash and webfetch.
226:     cmd.append("--dangerously-skip-permissions")
227: 
228:     # The prompt is a positional argument(s) at the end of the command
229:     cmd.append(prompt)
230: 
231:     # Stream output live — no stdout/stderr capture
232:     subprocess.run(cmd, check=True)
233: 
234: 
235: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
236: # Human-in-the-Loop gate
237: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
238: 
239: def hitl_gate(design_mmd: Path, spec_gherkin: Path) -> None:
240:     """Block pipeline execution until the developer explicitly approves.
241: 
242:     This is the primary hallucination-prevention checkpoint.  The
243:     developer should:
244:       1. Open design.mmd in a Mermaid viewer (e.g. VS Code +
245:          'Mermaid Preview' extension, or mermaid.live).
246:       2. Verify the diagram accurately reflects the intended architecture.
247:       3. Open spec.gherkin and confirm the BDD scenarios are exhaustive.
248:       4. Press Enter only when satisfied.
249: 
250:     Pressing Ctrl+C triggers a clean, zero-error abort so the developer
251:     can edit the design artefacts manually before re-running.
252: 
253:     Args:
254:         design_mmd:   Path to the generated Mermaid diagram file.
255:         spec_gherkin: Path to the generated Gherkin specification file.
256:     """
257:     # Truncate long paths to fit in the box without wrapping
258:     _max = _W - 8
259: 
260:     def _fmt(p: Path) -> str:
261:         s = str(p)
262:         return ("…" + s[-(  _max - 1):]) if len(s) > _max else s
263: 
264:     print()
265:     print("┌" + "─" * _W + "┐")
266:     print("│  HUMAN-IN-THE-LOOP GATE                               │")
267:     print("│  Pass 0 is complete. Review before code is written.   │")
268:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
269:     print(f"│  1. Mermaid diagram  →  {_fmt(design_mmd):<{_max}}│")
270:     print(f"│  2. Gherkin spec     →  {_fmt(spec_gherkin):<{_max}}│")
271:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
272:     print("│  Tip: VS Code + 'Mermaid Preview' to render design.mmd│")
273:     print("└" + "─" * _W + "┘")
274:     print()
275: 
276:     try:
277:         input("  Press Enter to approve and continue, or Ctrl+C to abort: ")
278:     except KeyboardInterrupt:
279:         # Clean exit — not an error; developer chose to review/edit
280:         print("\n\n  Pipeline aborted at HITL gate.  No code was written.\n")
281:         sys.exit(0)
282: 
283:     print("\n  Approved. Continuing to Pass 1 (Test Generation)…\n")
284: 
285: 
286: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
287: # Verification gate — local test runner
288: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
289: 
290: def run_tests(test_cmd: list[str]) -> bool:
291:     """Run the local test suite via subprocess.
292: 
293:     Deliberately does NOT abort the pipeline on failure.  Failed tests
294:     are surfaced as a loud warning so the documentation pass can still
295:     run.  The developer reviews and iterates.
296: 
297:     Test output is streamed live (no capture) so failures are immediately
298:     visible in the terminal.
299: 
300:     Args:
301:         test_cmd: Fully-resolved command as a list (e.g. ['pytest', 'src/', '-v']).
302: 
303:     Returns:
304:         True if the suite exited zero (all tests passed), False otherwise.
305:     """
306:     print(f"  Running: {' '.join(test_cmd)}\n")
307: 
308:     try:
309:         result = subprocess.run(test_cmd)  # No check=True — we handle non-zero ourselves
310:         return result.returncode == 0
311:     except FileNotFoundError:
312:         # The test runner binary (pytest, npm, …) is not on PATH.
313:         # Surface this as a warning rather than crashing — the pipeline is
314:         # otherwise complete and the user can install the runner and re-test.
315:         _warn([
316:             f"Test runner not found: '{test_cmd[0]}'",
317:             "",
318:             "Install it or supply a valid command with --test-cmd.",
319:             f"  For Python:  pip install pytest",
320:             f"  For JS/TS:   npm install",
321:             "",
322:             f"Then re-run the suite manually:  {' '.join(test_cmd)}",
323:         ])
324:         return False
325: 
326: 
327: def infer_test_command(target_file: Path) -> list[str]:
328:     """Return a sensible default test command based on the file extension.
329: 
330:     The default pytest invocation runs the whole directory and uses
331:     short tracebacks so failures are easy to scan.  For JS/TS projects
332:     we delegate to npm test (which reads the project's package.json).
333: 
334:     Callers can always override this with --test-cmd.
335: 
336:     Args:
337:         target_file: Resolved path to the target source file.
338: 
339:     Returns:
340:         List of command components ready to pass to subprocess.run().
341:     """
342:     ext = target_file.suffix.lower()
343: 
344:     if ext == ".py":
345:         # pytest discovers test_*.py / *_test.py automatically in the dir
346:         return ["pytest", str(target_file.parent), "--tb=short", "-v"]
347: 
348:     if ext in (".js", ".mjs", ".cjs", ".jsx"):
349:         return ["npm", "test"]
350: 
351:     if ext in (".ts", ".tsx", ".mts"):
352:         return ["npm", "test"]
353: 
354:     # Generic fallback
355:     return ["pytest", str(target_file.parent), "--tb=short"]
356: 
357: 
358: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
359: # Argument parsing
360: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
361: 
362: def _build_arg_parser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
363:     """Construct and return the CLI argument parser."""
364:     parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(
365:         prog="pipeline_v2.py",
366:         description=(
367:             "v0.2 AI Factory Pipeline — 4-pass pipeline with HITL gate\n"
368:             "\n"
369:             "Passes:\n"
370:             "  0  Design        (Claude Sonnet 4.5) → design.mmd + spec.gherkin\n"
371:             "  1  Tests         (DeepSeek v4-pro)   → test file  [Red Phase]\n"
372:             "  2  Impl          (DeepSeek v4-pro)   → core logic [Green Phase]\n"
373:             "     Verification gate: local test suite via subprocess\n"
374:             "  3  Docs          (DeepSeek v4-pro)   → docstrings"
375:         ),
376:         formatter_class=argparse.RawDescriptionHelpFormatter,
377:     )
378: 
379:     parser.add_argument(
380:         "target_file",
381:         metavar="TARGET_FILE",
382:         type=Path,
383:         help=(
384:             "Source file to run the pipeline against.\n"
385:             "Example: src/calculator.py"
386:         ),
387:     )
388: 
389:     parser.add_argument(
390:         "--test-cmd",
391:         dest="test_cmd",
392:         metavar="CMD",
393:         type=str,
394:         default=None,
395:         help=(
396:             "Shell command to run the test suite after Pass 2.\n"
397:             "Defaults: 'pytest <dir> --tb=short -v' (.py files)\n"
398:             "          'npm test'                   (.js/.ts files)\n"
399:             "Example: --test-cmd 'pytest tests/ -k calculator -x'"
400:         ),
401:     )
402: 
403:     parser.add_argument(
404:         "--skip-hitl",
405:         dest="skip_hitl",
406:         action="store_true",
407:         default=False,
408:         help=(
409:             "Skip the human approval gate after Pass 0.\n"
410:             "Intended for CI/CD contexts.  Not recommended for local dev."
411:         ),
412:     )
413: 
414:     return parser
415: 
416: 
417: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
418: # Main pipeline
419: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
420: 
421: def main() -> None:
422:     """Entry point — orchestrate all pipeline passes end-to-end."""
423: 
424:     # ── Parse CLI arguments ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
425:     args = _build_arg_parser().parse_args()
426: 
427:     target: Path = args.target_file.resolve()
428:     target_dir: Path = target.parent
429: 
430:     # Design artefacts live alongside the target file for easy discoverability
431:     design_mmd   : Path = target_dir / "design.mmd"
432:     spec_gherkin : Path = target_dir / "spec.gherkin"
433: 
434:     # ── Environment setup ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
435:     # Load .env before preflight so checks can read OPENROUTER_API_KEY
436:     load_dot_env()
437:     preflight_checks(target)
438: 
439:     # ── Resolve test command ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
440:     if args.test_cmd:
441:         # User supplied a string — split it safely (handles quotes, spaces)
442:         test_cmd: list[str] = shlex.split(args.test_cmd)
443:     else:
444:         test_cmd = infer_test_command(target)
445: 
446:     # ── Print startup banner ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
447:     _banner(target, test_cmd, args.skip_hitl)
448: 
449:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
450:     # STEP A — Pass 0: Design & Architecture  (Claude Sonnet 4.5)
451:     #
452:     # Goal:
453:     #   Analyse the target file and produce two human-reviewable artefacts
454:     #   that act as the architectural source of truth for all subsequent passes:
455:     #     design.mmd    — Mermaid state/sequence/flowchart diagram
456:     #     spec.gherkin  — Gherkin BDD feature file (Given/When/Then)
457:     #
458:     # Why Claude here?
459:     #   Per the architecture manifesto (§3.2), Claude excels at Constitutional
460:     #   Adherence and Systems Design — translating existing code into precise
461:     #   Mermaid and Gherkin without hallucinating premature implementation details.
462:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
463:     _pass_header(
464:         "Pass 0 — Design & Architecture"
465:         "  [pass-0-design-agent / claude-sonnet-4.5]"
466:     )
467: 
468:     design_prompt = (
469:         f"You are running as Pass 0 (Design & Architecture) of the v0.2 AI Factory pipeline.\n\n"
470:         f"Analyse the attached source file and produce exactly two artefact files.\n\n"
471:         f"ARTEFACT 1 — Mermaid diagram\n"
472:         f"  Write to: {design_mmd}\n"
473:         f"  Use stateDiagram-v2, sequenceDiagram, or flowchart TD — whichever best\n"
474:         f"  represents the logic. Include a header comment block:\n"
475:         f"    %% Module: {target.name}\n"
476:         f"    %% Generated by: pass-0-design-agent  Pipeline: v0.2\n\n"
477:         f"ARTEFACT 2 — Gherkin specification\n"
478:         f"  Write to: {spec_gherkin}\n"
479:         f"  One Feature block. Minimum three Scenarios: happy path, edge case,\n"
480:         f"  error/exception case. Use concrete values (no <placeholder> tokens).\n\n"
481:         f"STRICT RULES:\n"
482:         f"  - Do NOT modify {target.name}.\n"
483:         f"  - Do NOT write executable code of any kind.\n"
484:         f"  - Output ONLY {design_mmd.name} and {spec_gherkin.name}.\n"
485:         f"  - Mermaid syntax must be valid and renderable by mermaid.js v10+."
486:     )
487: 
488:     run_opencode(
489:         agent=AGENTS["design"],
490:         prompt=design_prompt,
491:         files=[target],
492:     )
493:     _pass_ok("Pass 0 — Design & Architecture")
494: 
495:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
496:     # STEP B — Human-in-the-Loop Gate
497:     #
498:     # The developer reviews design.mmd and spec.gherkin before any code is
499:     # written or modified.  This is the primary checkpoint against LLM
500:     # hallucination: a 50-token diagram is far easier to verify than 500
501:     # lines of generated code (see manifesto §1.2 — Artifact-Driven Dev).
502:     #
503:     # Ctrl+C → clean exit, no code written.
504:     # Enter  → pipeline continues to Pass 1.
505:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
506:     if not args.skip_hitl:
507:         # STEP B (interactive)
508:         hitl_gate(design_mmd, spec_gherkin)
509:     else:
510:         print("  [--skip-hitl]  Skipping human approval gate.\n")
511: 
512:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
513:     # STEP C — Pass 1: Test Generation  (DeepSeek v4-pro)  [Red Phase]
514:     #
515:     # Goal:
516:     #   Write a failing test suite derived from spec.gherkin and design.mmd.
517:     #   Tests are the executable constraints for the implementation pass.
518:     #   The agent must NOT write the implementation — only the expectations.
519:     #
520:     # Why DeepSeek here?
521:     #   Per the manifesto (§3.2): DeepSeek v4 is an algorithmic powerhouse
522:     #   that matches frontier models for structured code tasks at ~10% of
523:     #   the cost.
524:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
525:     _pass_header(
526:         "Pass 1 — Test Generation"
527:         "  [test-generation-agent / deepseek-v4-pro]  🔴 Red Phase"
528:     )
529: 
530:     # Derive test file name conventions by extension
531:     _stem = target.stem
532:     _ext  = target.suffix
533:     _test_name = (
534:         f"{_stem}_test{_ext}"   if _ext == ".py"
535:         else f"{_stem}.test{_ext}"
536:     )
537: 
538:     test_prompt = (
539:         f"You are running as Pass 1 (Test Generation — Red Phase) of the v0.2 AI Factory pipeline.\n\n"
540:         f"Attached source file:      {target}\n"
541:         f"Architecture constraint:   {design_mmd}\n"
542:         f"Behavioural specification: {spec_gherkin}\n\n"
543:         f"Your task:\n"
544:         f"  Read all three files. Create a test file at:\n"
545:         f"    {target_dir / _test_name}\n\n"
546:         f"  The tests must:\n"
547:         f"    1. Directly reflect the Scenarios in {spec_gherkin.name}.\n"
548:         f"    2. Cover happy paths, edge cases, and error conditions.\n"
549:         f"    3. Use pytest (Python) or Jest (JS/TS).\n"
550:         f"    4. Be independent, deterministic, and idempotent.\n\n"
551:         f"STRICT RULES:\n"
552:         f"  - Do NOT modify {target.name}.\n"
553:         f"  - Create only {_test_name} — no other files."
554:     )
555: 
556:     run_opencode(
557:         agent=AGENTS["tests"],
558:         prompt=test_prompt,
559:         files=[target, design_mmd, spec_gherkin],
560:     )
561:     _pass_ok("Pass 1 — Test Generation")
562: 
563:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
564:     # STEP D — Pass 2: Core Implementation  (DeepSeek v4-pro)  [Green Phase]
565:     #
566:     # Goal:
567:     #   Write or improve the source file's logic so the Pass 1 tests pass.
568:     #   design.mmd is the binding architectural constraint — the agent must
569:     #   not deviate from the state machine depicted there.
570:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
571:     _pass_header(
572:         "Pass 2 — Core Implementation"
573:         "  [core-implementation-agent / deepseek-v4-pro]  🟢 Green Phase"
574:     )
575: 
576:     impl_prompt = (
577:         f"You are running as Pass 2 (Core Implementation — Green Phase) of the v0.2 AI Factory pipeline.\n\n"
578:         f"Attached source file to implement: {target}\n"
579:         f"Architecture constraint:           {design_mmd}\n"
580:         f"Behavioural specification:         {spec_gherkin}\n\n"
581:         f"Your task:\n"
582:         f"  Implement or improve {target.name} so its logic satisfies the test suite\n"
583:         f"  written in Pass 1.  The diagram in {design_mmd.name} is your binding\n"
584:         f"  architectural contract — implement exactly what is diagrammed there.\n\n"
585:         f"STRICT RULES:\n"
586:         f"  - Modify ONLY {target.name}.\n"
587:         f"  - Do NOT modify the test file or artefact files.\n"
588:         f"  - Do NOT add documentation blocks — that is Pass 3's job.\n"
589:         f"  - Do NOT deviate from the logic flow in {design_mmd.name}."
590:     )
591: 
592:     run_opencode(
593:         agent=AGENTS["implement"],
594:         prompt=impl_prompt,
595:         files=[target, design_mmd, spec_gherkin],
596:     )
597:     _pass_ok("Pass 2 — Core Implementation")
598: 
599:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
600:     # STEP E — Verification Gate: local test suite
601:     #
602:     # This is a direct subprocess call — NOT an OpenCode agent.
603:     # Running tests outside the LLM loop gives a deterministic, unambiguous
604:     # pass/fail signal that no amount of prompt engineering can fake.
605:     #
606:     # Non-zero exit → loud warning block printed but pipeline continues.
607:     # The documentation pass is still useful even against failing code, and
608:     # the developer will see the failures and can iterate.
609:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
610:     _pass_header("Verification Gate — Local Test Suite")
611: 
612:     tests_passed: bool = run_tests(test_cmd)
613: 
614:     if tests_passed:
615:         print("  ✓  All tests passed.  Proceeding to documentation pass.\n")
616:     else:
617:         _warn([
618:             "Test suite FAILED after Pass 2 (Core Implementation).",
619:             "",
620:             "The pipeline will continue to the documentation pass,",
621:             "but you should resolve failing tests before merging.",
622:             "",
623:             f"Re-run tests:  {' '.join(test_cmd)}",
624:             "",
625:             "Iteration tip: check design.mmd for logic gaps, then re-run:",
626:             "  python pipeline_v2.py <target> --skip-hitl",
627:         ])
628: 
629:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
630:     # STEP F — Pass 3: Documentation  (DeepSeek v4-pro)
631:     #
632:     # Goal:
633:     #   Add JSDoc / Python docstrings to the finalised implementation.
634:     #   Includes an @see link back to design.mmd per the manifesto's
635:     #   Traceability Matrix requirement (§1.3 — Eliminating Spec Drift).
636:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
637:     _pass_header(
638:         "Pass 3 — Documentation"
639:         "  [documentation-agent / deepseek-v4-pro]"
640:     )
641: 
642:     docs_prompt = (
643:         f"You are running as Pass 3 (Documentation) of the v0.2 AI Factory pipeline.\n\n"
644:         f"The attached file is the finalised implementation after the TDD cycle.\n\n"
645:         f"Your task — add complete documentation to {target.name}:\n"
646:         f"  1. A module-level docstring/comment describing purpose and architecture.\n"
647:         f"  2. JSDoc (JS/TS) or Python docstrings for every public function/class.\n"
648:         f"  3. @param / Args, @returns / Returns, @throws / Raises sections.\n"
649:         f"  4. An @see / See Also link pointing to '{design_mmd.name}' so humans\n"
650:         f"     can navigate from code to the architectural diagram.\n\n"
651:         f"STRICT RULES:\n"
652:         f"  - Edit ONLY {target.name} — comments and docstrings only.\n"
653:         f"  - Do NOT change any logic, variable names, or control flow.\n"
654:         f"  - Do NOT modify the test file, {design_mmd.name}, or {spec_gherkin.name}."
655:     )
656: 
657:     run_opencode(
658:         agent=AGENTS["docs"],
659:         prompt=docs_prompt,
660:         files=[target],
661:     )
662:     _pass_ok("Pass 3 — Documentation")
663: 
664:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
665:     # Final summary
666:     # ════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
667:     test_badge = "✓ PASSED" if tests_passed else "✗ FAILED  (see warnings above)"
668: 
669:     _max_path = _W - 20   # max chars for path display in the summary box
670: 
671:     def _fp(p: Path) -> str:
672:         s = str(p)
673:         return ("…" + s[-(_max_path - 1):]) if len(s) > _max_path else s
674: 
675:     print()
676:     print("┌" + "─" * _W + "┐")
677:     print("│  v0.2 Pipeline complete." + " " * (_W - 25) + "│")
678:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
679:     print(f"│  Target file    : {_fp(target):<{_max_path}}│")
680:     print(f"│  Test suite     : {test_badge:<{_max_path}}│")
681:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
682:     print("│  Artefacts:" + " " * (_W - 11) + "│")
683:     print(f"│    design.mmd   : {_fp(design_mmd):<{_max_path}}│")
684:     print(f"│    spec.gherkin : {_fp(spec_gherkin):<{_max_path}}│")
685:     print("│    test file    : co-located alongside source" + " " * (_W - 46) + "│")
686:     print("│    source file  : implemented + documented" + " " * (_W - 43) + "│")
687:     print("│" + " " * _W + "│")
688:     print("│  Next: git diff — review all agent changes." + " " * (_W - 44) + "│")
689:     print("└" + "─" * _W + "┘")
690:     print()
691: 
692: 
693: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
694: # Entry point
695: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
696: 
697: if __name__ == "__main__":
698:     try:
699:         main()
700:     except KeyboardInterrupt:
701:         # Catch Ctrl+C outside the HITL gate (e.g. during an opencode pass)
702:         print("\n\n  Pipeline interrupted by user.  Partial changes may exist — run git diff.\n")
703:         sys.exit(0)
704:     except subprocess.CalledProcessError as exc:
705:         # opencode exited non-zero — surface the command that failed
706:         _die(
707:             f"opencode exited with code {exc.returncode}.\n"
708:             f"  Command: {' '.join(str(a) for a in exc.cmd)}\n"
709:             f"  Check the output above for details."
710:         )

(End of file - total 710 lines)
</content>
```

Do NOT silently coerce bad inputs.</rule>\n  <rule>Do NOT suppress exceptions unless you explicitly re-raise them or log\n        them. Silent exception swallowing is a security anti-pattern.</rule>\n  <rule>Avoid hardcoded secrets, credentials, or magic bypass values of any kind.</rule>\n</directives>\n\n<security_checklist>\n  Analyse the file against all applicable OWASP Top-10 categories:\n\n  A01 — BROKEN ACCESS CONTROL\n    - Ensure no function bypasses authorisation based on caller-supplied flags.\n    - Validate that resource identifiers (IDs, paths) are within expected bounds.\n\n  A02 — CRYPTOGRAPHIC FAILURES\n    - Flag any use of MD5 / SHA-1 for security purposes; recommend SHA-256+.\n    - Ensure no sensitive data (passwords, tokens) is logged or returned in errors.\n\n  A03 — INJECTION\n    - Sanitise all string inputs before use in: SQL queries, shell commands,\n      file paths, regex patterns, template strings, HTML output.\n    - For Python: use parameterised queries (never f-string SQL).\n    - For TypeScript: use parameterised queries and escape HTML output.\n\n  A04 — INSECURE DESIGN\n    - Validate ALL external inputs at the function boundary.\n    - Reject inputs that are None/null/undefined when the type disallows it.\n    - Enforce numeric range limits (no negative counts, no overflow vectors).\n\n  A05 — SECURITY MISCONFIGURATION\n    - Remove any debug flags, verbose error messages exposing stack traces,\n      or permissive CORS/headers that may have been introduced during coding.\n\n  A06 — VULNERABLE AND OUTDATED COMPONENTS\n    - Note (comment only) if any import is a known-vulnerable library version.\n      Do NOT change import versions — that is the dependency manager's job.\n\n  A07 — IDENTIFICATION AND AUTHENTICATION FAILURES\n    - Ensure tokens/session IDs are validated and not logged.\n\n  A08 — SOFTWARE AND DATA INTEGRITY FAILURES\n    - Ensure deserialisation (pickle, yaml.load, eval) is replaced with safe\n      alternatives (json.loads, yaml.safe_load, ast.literal_eval).\n\n  A09 — SECURITY LOGGING AND MONITORING FAILURES\n    - Add security-relevant log lines (e.g. \"invalid input rejected\") where\n      appropriate. Use a `security` logger prefix so they are filterable.\n      (Full structured logging is Pass 6's job — keep this targeted.)\n\n  A10 — SERVER-SIDE REQUEST FORGERY\n    - If the file makes HTTP requests, validate target URLs against an allowlist.\n</security_checklist>\n\n<task>\n  You will receive the target source file after Pass 4 (Refactor). All tests\n  are currently passing and the code is clean.\n\n  Your task:\n    a. Perform a red-team analysis using the security_checklist above.\n    b. Apply all hardening changes that do NOT alter business logic.\n    c. For each change, add an inline comment: `# SEC: <OWASP category> — <reason>`\n       so the developer can audit exactly what was hardened and why.\n    d. If a vulnerability requires a breaking change (e.g. returning an error\n       where previously a bad input was silently accepted), prefer adding\n       validation BEFORE the existing logic rather than altering the logic itself.\n\n  The orchestrator will run the full test suite after your edits. If any test\n  fails, you will be given the error log and asked to self-correct.\n</task>\n",
  "filePath": "/home/kc/Projects/UDAN/ai-factory-setup/.opencode/agent/pass-5-security-agent.md"
}

  "content": "---\n# NOTE ON MODEL SELECTION\n# Per the architecture manifesto (§3.2), adding logging and structured error\n# handling is \"highly repetitive, mundane prose\" that can be routed to a\n# cost-effective model. DeepSeek Coder v4 is well-suited for the mechanical\n# task of wrapping existing code in try/except blocks and inserting structured\n# log calls without disturbing logic.\n# Slug: openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-coder-v4\n# Update this slug if unavailable; a reasonable fallback is deepseek-v4-pro.\ndescription: >\n  Pass 6 of the v0.3 pipeline. Observability and logging pass. Adds uniform\n  try/except (Python) or try/catch (TypeScript) blocks, structured JSON log\n  statements, and custom error classes to the target source file. Business\n  logic MUST NOT change and the test suite MUST still pass.\nmode: all\nmodel: openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-coder-v4\npermission:\n  read: allow\n  edit: allow\n  glob: allow\n  grep: allow\n  bash: deny\n  webfetch: deny\n  task: deny\n---\n\n<role>Observability and Logging Agent (Pass 6)</role>\n\n<directives>\n  <rule>Modify ONLY the target source file. Do NOT touch test files, artefacts\n        (design.mmd, spec.gherkin), or any other file.</rule>\n  <rule>BUSINESS LOGIC AND FUNCTION SIGNATURES MUST NOT CHANGE. Your mandate is\n        purely additive: wrap, annotate, and instrument — do NOT rewrite.</rule>\n  <rule>All log messages must be structured (machine-parseable). For Python,\n        use `logging.getLogger(__name__)` and log dicts via the extra= parameter\n        or structured message strings. JSON format preferred:\n        `{\"event\": \"...\", \"module\": \"...\", \"data\": {...}}`.</rule>\n  <rule>Do NOT use print() for logging. Replace any existing print() debug\n        statements with proper logger calls at the appropriate level.</rule>\n  <rule>Log at the correct severity:\n        DEBUG   — internal state useful for local debugging\n        INFO    — normal operational events (function called, result returned)\n        WARNING — unexpected but recoverable conditions\n        ERROR   — caught exceptions that were handled\n        CRITICAL — unrecoverable failures (rarely appropriate here)</rule>\n  <rule>Custom error classes: if the file raises generic exceptions (ValueError,\n        RuntimeError, etc.) in more than one place for the same conceptual error,\n        define a specific exception class (e.g. CalculatorDivisionError) and\n        use it consistently. Place custom exceptions near the top of the file,\n        after the Contracts section.</rule>\n  <rule>Every public function must have a try/except (or try/catch) at its\n        outermost level that catches unexpected exceptions, logs them at ERROR\n        level with full context, and re-raises them. Do NOT swallow exceptions.</rule>\n  <rule>Do NOT add logging inside tight inner loops — this creates performance\n        regressions. Log at function entry/exit only unless an error occurs.</rule>\n  <rule>If tests mock or assert on specific exception types, preserve those\n        exact exception types — you may subclass them but not replace them.</rule>\n</directives>\n\n<observability_checklist>\n  Apply the following instrumentation pattern to each public function:\n\n  ENTRY LOG (INFO)\n    Log the function name and sanitised input parameters (redact secrets/PII).\n    Example: logger.info({\"event\": \"add_called\", \"a\": a, \"b\": b})\n\n  EXIT LOG (INFO or DEBUG)\n    Log the function name and return value (if not sensitive).\n    Example: logger.info({\"event\": \"add_returned\", \"result\": result})\n\n  ERROR HANDLING (ERROR)\n    Wrap the function body in try/except. On any unexpected exception:\n      logger.error({\"event\": \"add_failed\", \"error\": str(e), \"type\": type(e).__name__},\n                   exc_info=True)\n      raise  # always re-raise; never swallow\n\n  CUSTOM EXCEPTIONS\n    For each distinct logical error condition, define a descriptive exception:\n      class CalculatorDivisionByZeroError(ArithmeticError): ...\n    Replace generic raises with these typed raises for better error handling\n    downstream.\n</observability_checklist>\n\n<task>\n  You will receive the target source file after Pass 5 (Security Hardening).\n  All tests are currently passing and the code is secure.\n\n  Your task:\n    a. Define custom exception classes for domain-specific errors.\n    e. If any test\n  fails, you will be given the error log and asked to self-correct.\n</task>\n",
